---
collectionId: "9ktkng9a95n6199"
collectionName: "projects"
created: "2023-06-14 06:09:34.900Z"
description: "<p>An&nbsp;<strong>artificial general intelligence</strong>&nbsp;(<strong>AGI</strong>) is a type of hypothetical&nbsp;<a title=\"Intelligent agent\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent\">intelligent agent</a>. The AGI concept is that it can learn to accomplish any intellectual task that&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Human beings\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_beings\">human beings</a>&nbsp;or animals can perform.<sup id=\"cite_ref-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-1\">[1]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:10_2-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:10-2\">[2]</a></sup>&nbsp;Alternatively, AGI has been defined as an autonomous system that surpasses human capabilities in the majority of economically valuable tasks.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:1_3-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:1-3\">[3]</a></sup>&nbsp;Creating AGI is a primary goal of some&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence\">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;research and companies such as&nbsp;<a title=\"OpenAI\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenAI\">OpenAI</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-:1_3-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:1-3\">[3]</a></sup>&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"DeepMind\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeepMind\">DeepMind</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Anthropic\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthropic\">Anthropic</a>. AGI is a common topic in&nbsp;<a title=\"Science fiction\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_fiction\">science fiction</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Futures studies\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Futures_studies\">futures studies</a>.</p>\r\n<p>The timeline for AGI development remains a subject of ongoing debate among researchers and experts. Some argue that it may be possible in years or decades, others maintain it might take a century or longer, and a minority believe it may never be achieved.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:2_5-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:2-5\">[5]</a></sup>&nbsp;Additionally, there is debate regarding whether modern deep learning systems, such as&nbsp;<a title=\"GPT-4\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GPT-4\">GPT-4</a>, are an early yet incomplete form of AGI<sup id=\"cite_ref-:11_6-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:11-6\">[6]</a></sup>&nbsp;or if new approaches are required.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:3_7-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:3-7\">[7]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Contention exists over the potential for AGI to pose a threat to humanity; for example, OpenAI treats it as an&nbsp;<a title=\"Existential risk from artificial general intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Existential_risk_from_artificial_general_intelligence\">existential risk</a>, while others find the development of AGI to be too remote to present a risk.<sup id=\"cite_ref-8\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-8\">[8]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:2_5-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:2-5\">[5]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:3_7-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:3-7\">[7]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>A 2020 survey identified 72 active AGI&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"R&amp;D\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%26D\">R&amp;D</a>&nbsp;projects spread across 37 countries.<sup id=\"cite_ref-baum_9-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-baum-9\">[9]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Terminology\" class=\"mw-headline\">Terminology</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Terminology\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<p>AGI is also known as strong AI,<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKurzweil2005260_10-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKurzweil2005260-10\">[10]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Kurzweil_2005-08-05_11-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Kurzweil_2005-08-05-11\">[11]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-12\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>&nbsp;full AI,<sup id=\"cite_ref-13\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>&nbsp;or general intelligent action.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTENewellSimon1976_14-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTENewellSimon1976-14\">[14]</a></sup>&nbsp;However, some academic sources reserve the term \"strong AI\" for computer programs that experience&nbsp;<a title=\"Sentience\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sentience\">sentience</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title=\"Consciousness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness\">consciousness</a>.&nbsp;<sup id=\"cite_ref-Searle's_Strong_AI_15-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Searle's_Strong_AI-15\">[a]</a></sup>&nbsp;In contrast, weak AI (or narrow AI) is able to solve one specific problem, but lacks general cognitive abilities.<sup id=\"cite_ref-16\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-16\">[15]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Kurzweil_2005-08-05_11-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Kurzweil_2005-08-05-11\">[11]</a></sup>&nbsp;Some academic sources use \"weak AI\" to refer more broadly to any programs that neither experience consciousness nor have a mind in the same sense as humans.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Searle's_Strong_AI_15-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Searle's_Strong_AI-15\">[a]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Related concepts include human-level AI, transformative AI,<sup id=\"cite_ref-:2_5-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:2-5\">[5]</a></sup>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Superintelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superintelligence\">superintelligence</a>.</p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Characteristics\" class=\"mw-headline\">Characteristics</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Characteristics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article:&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence\">Artificial intelligence</a></div>\r\n<p>Various criteria for&nbsp;<a title=\"Intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence\">intelligence</a>&nbsp;have been proposed (most famously the&nbsp;<a title=\"Turing test\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_test\">Turing test</a>) but no definition is broadly accepted.<sup id=\"cite_ref-18\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-18\">[b]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Intelligence_traits\" class=\"mw-headline\">Intelligence traits</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Intelligence traits\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>However, researchers generally hold that intelligence is required to do the following:<sup id=\"cite_ref-:12_19-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:12-19\">[17]</a></sup></p>\r\n<ul>\r\n<li><a title=\"Automated reasoning\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning\">reason</a>, use strategy, solve puzzles, and make judgments under&nbsp;<a title=\"Uncertainty\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncertainty\">uncertainty</a>;</li>\r\n<li><a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Knowledge representation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation\">represent knowledge</a>, including&nbsp;<a title=\"Commonsense knowledge (artificial intelligence)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonsense_knowledge_(artificial_intelligence)\">common sense knowledge</a>;</li>\r\n<li><a title=\"Automated planning and scheduling\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_planning_and_scheduling\">plan</a>;</li>\r\n<li><a title=\"Machine learning\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning\">learn</a>;</li>\r\n<li>communicate in&nbsp;<a title=\"Natural language processing\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_processing\">natural language</a>;</li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>and, if necessary,&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial intelligence systems integration\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence_systems_integration\">integrate these skills</a>&nbsp;in completion of any given goal.</p>\r\n<p>Many&nbsp;<a title=\"Interdisciplinarity\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinarity\">interdisciplinary</a>&nbsp;approaches (e.g.&nbsp;<a title=\"Cognitive science\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_science\">cognitive science</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Computational intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_intelligence\">computational intelligence</a>, and&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Decision making\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_making\">decision making</a>) consider additional traits such as&nbsp;<a title=\"Imagination\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imagination\">imagination</a>&nbsp;(the ability to form novel mental images and concepts)<sup id=\"cite_ref-20\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-20\">[18]</a></sup>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Self-determination theory\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-determination_theory\">autonomy</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-21\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-21\">[19]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Computer-based systems that exhibit many of these capabilities exist (e.g. see&nbsp;<a title=\"Computational creativity\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_creativity\">computational creativity</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Automated reasoning\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning\">automated reasoning</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Decision support system\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_support_system\">decision support system</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Robot\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robot\">robot</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Evolutionary computation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computation\">evolutionary computation</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Intelligent agent\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent\">intelligent agent</a>). However, no consensus holds that modern AI systems possess them to an adequate degree.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Physical_traits\" class=\"mw-headline\">Physical traits</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Physical traits\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>Other capabilities are considered desirable in intelligent systems, as they may affect intelligence or aid in its expression. These include:<sup id=\"cite_ref-:13_22-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:13-22\">[20]</a></sup></p>\r\n<ul>\r\n<li>the ability to&nbsp;<a title=\"Machine perception\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_perception\">sense</a>&nbsp;(e.g.&nbsp;<a title=\"Computer vision\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision\">see</a>, hear, etc.), and</li>\r\n<li>the ability to act (e.g.&nbsp;<a title=\"Robotics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics\">move and manipulate objects</a>, change location to explore, etc.)</li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>This includes the ability to detect and respond to&nbsp;<a title=\"Hazard\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazard\">hazard</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-23\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-23\">[21]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Mathematical_formalisms\" class=\"mw-headline\">Mathematical formalisms</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Mathematical formalisms\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>A mathematically precise specification of AGI was proposed by&nbsp;<a title=\"Marcus Hutter\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Hutter\">Marcus Hutter</a>&nbsp;in 2000. Named&nbsp;<a title=\"AIXI\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AIXI\">AIXI</a>, the proposed AGI agent maximises &ldquo;the ability to satisfy goals in a wide range of environments&rdquo;.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:14_24-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:14-24\">[22]</a></sup>&nbsp;This type of AGI, characterized by the ability to maximise a mathematical definition of intelligence rather than exhibit human-like behaviour,<sup id=\"cite_ref-25\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-25\">[23]</a></sup>&nbsp;is also called universal artificial intelligence.<sup id=\"cite_ref-26\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-26\">[24]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2015&nbsp;<a class=\"new\" title=\"Jan Lieke (page does not exist)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jan_Lieke&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1\">Jan Lieke</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Marcus Hutter\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Hutter\">Marcus Hutter</a>&nbsp;showed that Legg-Hutter intelligence - \"an agent&rsquo;s ability to achieve goals in a wide range of environments\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-27\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-27\">[25]</a></sup>&nbsp;- is measured with respect to \"a fixed Universal Turing Machine<a title=\"Universal Turing machine\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Turing_machine\">(UTM</a>). AIXI is the most intelligent policy if it uses the same UTM\", a result which \"undermines all existing optimality properties for AIXI\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-28\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-28\">[26]</a></sup>&nbsp;This problem stems from AIXI's use of compression as a proxy for intelligence, which is only valid if cognition takes place in isolation from the environment in which goals are pursued. This formalises a philosophical position known as&nbsp;<a title=\"Mind&ndash;body dualism\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind%E2%80%93body_dualism\">Mind&ndash;body dualism</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-&rdquo;mtb1&rdquo;_29-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-%E2%80%9Dmtb1%E2%80%9D-29\">[27]</a></sup>&nbsp;Some find&nbsp;<a title=\"Enactivism\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enactivism\">enactivism</a>&nbsp;more plausible&mdash;the notion that cognition takes place within the same environment in which goals are pursued.<sup id=\"cite_ref-30\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-30\">[28]</a></sup>&nbsp;Subsequently,&nbsp;<a class=\"new\" title=\"Michael Timothy Bennett (page does not exist)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Michael_Timothy_Bennett&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1\">Michael Timothy Bennett</a>&nbsp;formalised enactive cognition and identified an alternative proxy for intelligence called \"weakness\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-&rdquo;mtb1&rdquo;_29-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-%E2%80%9Dmtb1%E2%80%9D-29\">[27]</a></sup>&nbsp;The accompanying experiments (comparing weakness and compression) and mathematical proofs showed that maximising weakness results in the optimal \"ability to complete a wide range of tasks\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-&rdquo;mtb2&rdquo;_31-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-%E2%80%9Dmtb2%E2%80%9D-31\">[29]</a></sup>&nbsp;or equivalently \"ability to generalise\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-32\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-32\">[30]</a></sup>&nbsp;(thus maximising intelligence by either definition). If&nbsp;<a title=\"Enactivism\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enactivism\">enactivism</a>&nbsp;holds and&nbsp;<a title=\"Mind&ndash;body dualism\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind%E2%80%93body_dualism\">Mind&ndash;body dualism</a>&nbsp;does not, then compression is not necessary or sufficient for intelligence, calling into question widely held views on intelligence (see also&nbsp;<a title=\"Hutter Prize\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hutter_Prize\">Hutter Prize</a>).</p>\r\n<p>Whether an AGI that satisfies one of these formalizations exhibits human-like behaviour (such as the use of natural language) would depend on many factors,<sup id=\"cite_ref-33\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-33\">[31]</a></sup>&nbsp;for example the manner in which the agent is embodied,<sup id=\"cite_ref-&rdquo;mtb2&rdquo;_31-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-%E2%80%9Dmtb2%E2%80%9D-31\">[29]</a></sup>&nbsp;or whether it has a reward function that closely approximates human primitives of cognition like hunger, pain, and so forth.<sup id=\"cite_ref-34\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-34\">[32]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Tests_for_testing_human-level_AGI\" class=\"mw-headline\">Tests for testing human-level AGI<span id=\"Tests_for_confirming_human-level_AGI\" class=\"anchor\"></span></span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Tests for testing human-level AGI\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>Several tests meant to confirm human-level AGI have been considered, including:<sup id=\"cite_ref-35\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-35\">[33]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-36\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-36\">[34]</a></sup></p>\r\n<dl>\r\n<dt><a title=\"Turing test\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_test\">The Turing Test</a>&nbsp;(<a title=\"Alan Turing\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Turing\"><em>Turing</em></a>)</dt>\r\n<dd>A machine and a human both converse unseen with a second human, who must evaluate which of the two is the machine, which passes the test if it can fool the evaluator a significant fraction of the time. Note: Turing does not prescribe what should qualify as intelligence, only that knowing that it is a machine should disqualify it. The AI&nbsp;<a title=\"Eugene Goostman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_Goostman\">Eugene Goostman</a>&nbsp;achieved Turing's estimate of convincing 30% of judges that it was human in 2014.</dd>\r\n<dt>The Robot College Student Test (<a title=\"Ben Goertzel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Goertzel\"><em>Goertzel</em></a>)</dt>\r\n<dd>A machine enrolls in a university, taking and passing the same classes that humans would, and obtaining a degree. LLMs can now pass university degree-level exams without even attending the classes.<sup id=\"cite_ref-37\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-37\">[35]</a></sup></dd>\r\n<dt>The Employment Test (<a title=\"Nils John Nilsson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nils_John_Nilsson\"><em>Nilsson</em></a>)</dt>\r\n<dd>A machine performs an economically important job at least as well as humans in the same job. AIs are now replacing humans in many roles as varied as fast food, marketing, and software engineering.<sup id=\"cite_ref-38\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-38\">[36]</a></sup></dd>\r\n<dt>The Ikea test (<a title=\"Gary Marcus\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gary_Marcus\"><em>Marcus</em></a>)</dt>\r\n<dd>Also known as the Flat Pack Furniture Test. An AI views the parts and instructions of an Ikea flat-pack product, then controls a robot to assemble the furniture correctly.</dd>\r\n<dt>The Coffee Test (<a title=\"Steve Wozniak\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Wozniak\"><em>Wozniak</em></a>)</dt>\r\n<dd>A machine is required to enter an average American home and figure out how to make coffee: find the coffee machine, find the coffee, add water, find a mug, and brew the coffee by pushing the proper buttons. This has not yet been completed.</dd>\r\n</dl>\r\n<p>As each test is completed it is supplanted with others. The current state is that generalist AIs can surpass most trained humans at arbitrary degree-level exams, score in the top 0.1% of IQ tests,<sup id=\"cite_ref-39\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-39\">[37]</a></sup>&nbsp;and be so Turing-convincing that some of their own developers believe they're sentient,<sup id=\"cite_ref-40\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-40\">[38]</a></sup>&nbsp;all of which are general tasks for which they were not specifically trained, and yet the AIs are still not considered \"generally intelligent\"&nbsp;<em>enough</em>&nbsp;to be AGI.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"AI-complete_problems\" class=\"mw-headline\">AI-complete problems</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: AI-complete problems\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article:&nbsp;<a title=\"AI-complete\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI-complete\">AI-complete</a></div>\r\n<p>There are many problems that may require general intelligence, if machines are to solve the problems as well as people do. For example, even specific straightforward tasks, like&nbsp;<a title=\"Machine translation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_translation\">machine translation</a>, require that a machine read and write in both languages (<a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#Natural_language_processing\">NLP</a>), follow the author's argument (<a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#Deduction,_reasoning,_problem_solving\">reason</a>), know what is being talked about (<a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#Knowledge_representation\">knowledge</a>), and faithfully reproduce the author's original intent (<a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#Social_intelligence\">social intelligence</a>). All of these problems need to be solved simultaneously in order to reach human-level machine performance.</p>\r\n<p>A problem is informally called \"AI-complete\" or \"AI-hard\" if it is believed that to solve it one would need to implement strong AI, because the solution is beyond the capabilities of a purpose-specific algorithm.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Shapiro92_41-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Shapiro92-41\">[39]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>AI-complete problems are hypothesised to include general&nbsp;<a title=\"Computer vision\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision\">computer vision</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Natural-language understanding\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural-language_understanding\">natural language understanding</a>, and dealing with unexpected circumstances while solving any real-world problem.<sup id=\"cite_ref-42\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-42\">[40]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>AI-complete problems cannot be solved with current<sup class=\"noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact\">[<em><a title=\"Portal:Current events\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portal:Current_events\"><span title=\"This statement refers to current events and needs references to newer reliable sources. (April 2023)\">may be outdated as of April 2023</span></a></em>]</sup>&nbsp;computer technology alone, and require&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Human computation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_computation\">human computation</a>. This limitation could be useful to test for the presence of humans, as&nbsp;<a title=\"CAPTCHA\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CAPTCHA\">CAPTCHAs</a>&nbsp;aim to do; and for&nbsp;<a title=\"Computer security\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_security\">computer security</a>&nbsp;to repel&nbsp;<a title=\"Brute-force attack\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brute-force_attack\">brute-force attacks</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-43\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-43\">[41]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-44\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-44\">[42]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"History\" class=\"mw-headline\">History</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: History\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Classical_AI\" class=\"mw-headline\">Classical AI</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Classical AI\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main articles:&nbsp;<a title=\"History of artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_artificial_intelligence\">History of artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Symbolic artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbolic_artificial_intelligence\">Symbolic artificial intelligence</a></div>\r\n<p>Modern AI research began in the mid-1950s.<sup id=\"cite_ref-45\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-45\">[43]</a></sup>&nbsp;The first generation of AI researchers were convinced that artificial general intelligence was possible and that it would exist in just a few decades.<sup id=\"cite_ref-46\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-46\">[44]</a></sup>&nbsp;AI pioneer&nbsp;<a title=\"Herbert A. Simon\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_A._Simon\">Herbert A. Simon</a>&nbsp;wrote in 1965: \"machines will be capable, within twenty years, of doing any work a man can do.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-47\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-47\">[45]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Their predictions were the inspiration for&nbsp;<a title=\"Stanley Kubrick\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick\">Stanley Kubrick</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Arthur C. Clarke\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_C._Clarke\">Arthur C. Clarke</a>'s character&nbsp;<a title=\"HAL 9000\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HAL_9000\">HAL 9000</a>, who embodied what AI researchers believed they could create by the year 2001. AI pioneer&nbsp;<a title=\"Marvin Minsky\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvin_Minsky\">Marvin Minsky</a>&nbsp;was a consultant<sup id=\"cite_ref-48\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-48\">[46]</a></sup>&nbsp;on the project of making HAL 9000 as realistic as possible according to the consensus predictions of the time. He said in 1967, \"Within a generation... the problem of creating 'artificial intelligence' will substantially be solved\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-49\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-49\">[47]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Several&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Symbolic AI\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbolic_AI\">classical AI projects</a>, such as&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Doug Lenat\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doug_Lenat\">Doug Lenat</a>'s&nbsp;<a title=\"Cyc\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyc\">Cyc</a>&nbsp;project (that began in 1984), and&nbsp;<a title=\"Allen Newell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allen_Newell\">Allen Newell</a>'s&nbsp;<a title=\"Soar (cognitive architecture)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soar_(cognitive_architecture)\">Soar</a>&nbsp;project, were directed at AGI.</p>\r\n<p>However, in the early 1970s, it became obvious that researchers had grossly underestimated the difficulty of the project. Funding agencies became skeptical of AGI and put researchers under increasing pressure to produce useful \"applied AI\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-53\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-53\">[c]</a></sup>&nbsp;In the early 1980s, Japan's&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Fifth Generation Computer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fifth_Generation_Computer\">Fifth Generation Computer</a>&nbsp;Project revived interest in AGI, setting out a ten-year timeline that included AGI goals like \"carry on a casual conversation\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-54\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-54\">[51]</a></sup>&nbsp;In response to this and the success of&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Expert systems\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expert_systems\">expert systems</a>, both industry and government pumped money back into the field.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTENRC1999&quot;Shift_to_Applied_Research_Increases_Investment&quot;_51-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTENRC1999%22Shift_to_Applied_Research_Increases_Investment%22-51\">[49]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-55\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-55\">[52]</a></sup>&nbsp;However, confidence in AI spectacularly collapsed in the late 1980s, and the goals of the Fifth Generation Computer Project were never fulfilled.<sup id=\"cite_ref-56\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-56\">[53]</a></sup>&nbsp;For the second time in 20 years, AI researchers who predicted the imminent achievement of AGI had been mistaken. By the 1990s, AI researchers had a reputation for making vain promises. They became reluctant to make predictions at all<sup id=\"cite_ref-58\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-58\">[d]</a></sup>&nbsp;and avoided mention of \"human level\" artificial intelligence for fear of being labeled \"wild-eyed dreamer[s]\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-59\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-59\">[55]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Narrow_AI_research\" class=\"mw-headline\">Narrow AI research</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Narrow AI research\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article:&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence\">Artificial intelligence</a></div>\r\n<p>In the 1990s and early 21st century, mainstream AI achieved commercial success and academic respectability by focusing on specific sub-problems where AI can produce verifiable results and commercial applications, such as&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Artificial neural networks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_networks\">artificial neural networks</a>&nbsp;and statistical&nbsp;<a title=\"Machine learning\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning\">machine learning</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-60\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-60\">[56]</a></sup>&nbsp;These \"applied AI\" systems are now used extensively throughout the technology industry, and research in this vein is heavily funded in both academia and industry. As of 2018&nbsp;development on this field was considered an emerging trend, and a mature stage was expected to happen in more than 10 years.<sup id=\"cite_ref-61\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-61\">[57]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Most mainstream AI researchers<sup id=\"cite_ref-:4_62-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:4-62\">[58]</a></sup>&nbsp;hope that strong AI can be developed by combining programs that solve various sub-problems.&nbsp;<a title=\"Hans Moravec\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Moravec\">Hans Moravec</a>&nbsp;wrote in 1988:</p>\r\n<blockquote>\r\n<p>I am confident that this bottom-up route to artificial intelligence will one day meet the traditional top-down route more than half way, ready to provide the real world competence and the&nbsp;<a title=\"Commonsense knowledge (artificial intelligence)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonsense_knowledge_(artificial_intelligence)\">commonsense knowledge</a>&nbsp;that has been so frustratingly elusive in reasoning programs. Fully intelligent machines will result when the metaphorical&nbsp;<a title=\"Golden spike\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_spike\">golden spike</a>&nbsp;is driven uniting the two efforts.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:4_62-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:4-62\">[58]</a></sup></p>\r\n</blockquote>\r\n<p>However, this is disputed. For example, Stevan Harnad of Princeton University concluded his 1990 paper on the&nbsp;<a title=\"Symbol grounding problem\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbol_grounding_problem\">Symbol Grounding Hypothesis</a>&nbsp;by stating:</p>\r\n<blockquote>\r\n<p>The expectation has often been voiced that \"top-down\" (symbolic) approaches to modeling cognition will somehow meet \"bottom-up\" (sensory) approaches somewhere in between. If the grounding considerations in this paper are valid, then this expectation is hopelessly modular and there is really only one viable route from sense to symbols: from the ground up. A free-floating symbolic level like the software level of a computer will never be reached by this route (or vice versa) &ndash; nor is it clear why we should even try to reach such a level, since it looks as if getting there would just amount to uprooting our symbols from their intrinsic meanings (thereby merely reducing ourselves to the functional equivalent of a programmable computer).<sup id=\"cite_ref-63\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-63\">[59]</a></sup></p>\r\n</blockquote>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Modern_artificial_general_intelligence_research\" class=\"mw-headline\">Modern artificial general intelligence research</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Modern artificial general intelligence research\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>The term \"artificial general intelligence\" was used as early as 1997, by Mark Gubrud<sup id=\"cite_ref-64\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-64\">[60]</a></sup>&nbsp;in a discussion of the implications of fully automated military production and operations. The term was re-introduced and popularized by&nbsp;<a title=\"Shane Legg\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shane_Legg\">Shane Legg</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Ben Goertzel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Goertzel\">Ben Goertzel</a>&nbsp;around 2002.<sup id=\"cite_ref-65\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-65\">[61]</a></sup>&nbsp;AGI research activity in 2006 was described by Pei Wang and Ben Goertzel<sup id=\"cite_ref-66\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-66\">[62]</a></sup>&nbsp;as \"producing publications and preliminary results\". The first summer school in AGI was organized in Xiamen, China in 2009<sup id=\"cite_ref-67\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-67\">[63]</a></sup>&nbsp;by the Xiamen university's Artificial Brain Laboratory and OpenCog. The first university course was given in 2010<sup id=\"cite_ref-68\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-68\">[64]</a></sup>&nbsp;and 2011<sup id=\"cite_ref-69\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-69\">[65]</a></sup>&nbsp;at Plovdiv University, Bulgaria by Todor Arnaudov. MIT presented a course in AGI in 2018, organized by&nbsp;<a title=\"Lex Fridman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lex_Fridman\">Lex Fridman</a>&nbsp;and featuring a number of guest lecturers.</p>\r\n<p>As of 2023, a small number of computer scientists are active in AGI research, and many contribute to a series of&nbsp;<a title=\"Conference on Artificial General Intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conference_on_Artificial_General_Intelligence\">AGI conferences</a>. However, increasingly more researchers are interested in open-ended learning<sup id=\"cite_ref-70\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-70\">[66]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-71\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-71\">[67]</a></sup>, which is the idea of allowing AI to continuously learn and innovate like humans do. Although most open-ended learning works are still done on&nbsp;<a title=\"Minecraft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minecraft\">Minecraft</a><sup id=\"cite_ref-72\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-72\">[68]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-73\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-73\">[69]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-74\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-74\">[70]</a></sup>, its application can be extended to robotics and the sciences.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Feasibility\" class=\"mw-headline\">Feasibility</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Feasibility\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>As of 2022, AGI remains speculative.<sup id=\"cite_ref-spec1_75-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-spec1-75\">[71]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-spec2_76-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-spec2-76\">[72]</a></sup>&nbsp;No such system has yet been demonstrated. Opinions vary both on whether and when artificial general intelligence will arrive. AI pioneer&nbsp;<a title=\"Herbert A. Simon\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_A._Simon\">Herbert A. Simon</a>&nbsp;speculated in 1965 that \"machines will be capable, within twenty years, of doing any work a man can do\". This prediction failed to come true. Microsoft co-founder&nbsp;<a title=\"Paul Allen\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Allen\">Paul Allen</a>&nbsp;believed that such intelligence is unlikely in the 21st century because it would require \"unforeseeable and fundamentally unpredictable breakthroughs\" and a \"scientifically deep understanding of cognition\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-77\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-77\">[73]</a></sup>&nbsp;Writing in&nbsp;<em><a title=\"The Guardian\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian\">The Guardian</a></em>, roboticist Alan Winfield claimed the gulf between modern computing and human-level artificial intelligence is as wide as the gulf between current space flight and practical faster-than-light spaceflight.<sup id=\"cite_ref-78\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-78\">[74]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Most AI researchers believe strong AI can be achieved in the future, but some thinkers, like&nbsp;<a title=\"Hubert Dreyfus\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubert_Dreyfus\">Hubert Dreyfus</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Roger Penrose\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Penrose\">Roger Penrose</a>, deny the possibility of achieving strong AI.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClocksin2003_79-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClocksin2003-79\">[75]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:0_80-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:0-80\">[76]</a></sup>&nbsp;<a title=\"John McCarthy (computer scientist)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_McCarthy_(computer_scientist)\">John McCarthy</a>&nbsp;is among those who believe human-level AI will be accomplished, but that the present level of progress is such that a date cannot accurately be predicted.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCarthy2007_81-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCarthy2007-81\">[77]</a></sup>&nbsp;AI experts' views on the feasibility of AGI wax and wane. Four polls conducted in 2012 and 2013 suggested that the median guess among experts for when they would be 50% confident AGI would arrive was 2040 to 2050, depending on the poll, with the mean being 2081. Of the experts, 16.5% answered with \"never\" when asked the same question but with a 90% confidence instead.<sup id=\"cite_ref-new_yorker_doomsday_82-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-new_yorker_doomsday-82\">[78]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-83\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-83\">[79]</a></sup>&nbsp;Further current AGI progress considerations can be found above&nbsp;<a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#Tests_for_confirming_human-level_AGI\"><em>Tests for confirming human-level AGI</em></a>.</p>\r\n<p>A report by Stuart Armstrong and Kaj Sotala of the Machine Intelligence Research Institute found that \"over [a] 60 year time frame there is a strong bias towards predicting the arrival of human level AI as between 15 and 25 years from the time the prediction was made\". They analyzed 95 predictions made between 1950 and 2012 on when human level AI will come about.&nbsp;<sup id=\"cite_ref-84\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-84\">[80]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Timescales\" class=\"mw-headline\">Timescales</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Timescales\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>In the introduction to his 2006 book,<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoertzelPennachin2006_85-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoertzelPennachin2006-85\">[81]</a></sup>&nbsp;Goertzel says that estimates of the time needed before a truly flexible AGI is built vary from 10 years to over a century. As of 2007&nbsp;the consensus in the AGI research community seemed to be that the timeline discussed by&nbsp;<a title=\"Ray Kurzweil\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Kurzweil\">Ray Kurzweil</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<em><a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"The Singularity is Near\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Singularity_is_Near\">The Singularity is Near</a></em><sup id=\"cite_ref-K_86-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-K-86\">[82]</a></sup>&nbsp;(i.e. between 2015 and 2045) was plausible.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoertzel2007_87-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoertzel2007-87\">[83]</a></sup>&nbsp;Mainstream AI researchers have given a wide range of opinions on whether progress will be this rapid. A 2012 meta-analysis of 95 such opinions found a bias towards predicting that the onset of AGI would occur within 16&ndash;26 years for modern and historical predictions alike. That paper has been criticized for how it categorized opinions as expert or non-expert.<sup id=\"cite_ref-88\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-88\">[84]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2012,&nbsp;<a title=\"Alex Krizhevsky\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Krizhevsky\">Alex Krizhevsky</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Ilya Sutskever\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilya_Sutskever\">Ilya Sutskever</a>, and&nbsp;<a title=\"Geoffrey Hinton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoffrey_Hinton\">Geoffrey Hinton</a>&nbsp;developed a neural network called&nbsp;<a title=\"AlexNet\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AlexNet\">AlexNet</a>, which won the&nbsp;<a title=\"ImageNet\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ImageNet\">ImageNet</a>&nbsp;competition with a top-5 test error rate of 15.3%, significantly better than the second-best entry's rate of 26.3% (the traditional approach used a weighted sum of scores from different pre-defined classifiers).<sup id=\"cite_ref-:5_89-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:5-89\">[85]</a></sup>&nbsp;AlexNet was regarded as the initial ground-breaker of the current deep learning wave.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:5_89-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:5-89\">[85]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2017, researchers Feng Liu, Yong Shi, and Ying Liu conducted intelligence tests on publicly available and freely accessible weak AI such as Google AI, Apple's Siri, and others. At the maximum, these AIs reached an IQ value of about 47, which corresponds approximately to a six-year-old child in first grade. An adult comes to about 100 on average. Similar tests were carried out in 2014, with the IQ score reaching a maximum value of 27.<sup id=\"cite_ref-90\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-90\">[86]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-91\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-91\">[87]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2020,&nbsp;<a title=\"OpenAI\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenAI\">OpenAI</a>&nbsp;developed&nbsp;<a title=\"GPT-3\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GPT-3\">GPT-3</a>, a language model capable of performing many diverse tasks without specific training. According to&nbsp;<a title=\"Gary Grossman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gary_Grossman\">Gary Grossman</a>&nbsp;in a&nbsp;<a title=\"VentureBeat\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VentureBeat\">VentureBeat</a>&nbsp;article, while there is consensus that GPT-3 is not an example of AGI, it is considered by some to be too advanced to classify as a narrow AI system.<sup id=\"cite_ref-92\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-92\">[88]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In the same year, Jason Rohrer used his GPT-3 account to develop a chatbot, and provided a chatbot-developing platform called \"Project December\". OpenAI asked for changes to the chatbot to comply with their safety guidelines; Rohrer disconnected Project December from the GPT-3 API.<sup id=\"cite_ref-93\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-93\">[89]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2022,&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"DeepMind\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeepMind\">DeepMind</a>&nbsp;developed&nbsp;<a title=\"Gato (DeepMind)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gato_(DeepMind)\">Gato</a>, a \"general-purpose\" system capable of performing more than 600 different tasks.<sup id=\"cite_ref-94\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-94\">[90]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2023,&nbsp;<a title=\"Microsoft Research\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Research\">Microsoft Research</a>&nbsp;published a study on an early version of OpenAI's&nbsp;<a title=\"GPT-4\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GPT-4\">GPT-4</a>, contending that it exhibited more general intelligence than previous AI models and demonstrated human-level performance in tasks spanning multiple domains, such as mathematics, coding, and law. This research sparked a debate on whether GPT-4 could be considered an early, incomplete version of artificial general intelligence, emphasizing the need for further exploration and evaluation of such systems.<sup id=\"cite_ref-95\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-95\">[91]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2023, the AI researcher&nbsp;<a title=\"Geoffrey Hinton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoffrey_Hinton\">Geoffrey Hinton</a>&nbsp;stated that:<sup id=\"cite_ref-96\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-96\">[92]</a></sup></p>\r\n<blockquote class=\"templatequote\">\r\n<p>The idea that this stuff could actually get smarter than people &mdash; a few people believed that, [...]. But most people thought it was way off. And I thought it was way off. I thought it was 30 to 50 years or even longer away. Obviously, I no longer think that.</p>\r\n</blockquote>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Brain_simulation\" class=\"mw-headline\">Brain simulation</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Brain simulation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Whole_brain_emulation\" class=\"mw-headline\">Whole brain emulation</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Whole brain emulation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article:&nbsp;<a title=\"Mind uploading\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind_uploading\">Mind uploading</a></div>\r\n<p>One possible approach to achieving AGI is&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Whole brain emulation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whole_brain_emulation\">whole brain emulation</a>: A brain model is built by&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Brain scanning\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain_scanning\">scanning</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Brain mapping\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain_mapping\">mapping</a>&nbsp;a biological brain in detail and copying its state into a computer system or another computational device. The computer runs a&nbsp;<a title=\"Computer simulation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_simulation\">simulation</a>&nbsp;model sufficiently faithful to the original that it behaves in practically the same way as the original brain.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Roadmap_97-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Roadmap-97\">[93]</a></sup>&nbsp;Whole brain emulation is discussed in&nbsp;<a title=\"Computational neuroscience\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_neuroscience\">computational neuroscience</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Neuroinformatics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroinformatics\">neuroinformatics</a>, in the context of&nbsp;<a title=\"Brain simulation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain_simulation\">brain simulation</a>&nbsp;for medical research purposes. It is discussed in&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence\">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;research<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoertzel2007_87-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoertzel2007-87\">[83]</a></sup>&nbsp;as an approach to strong AI.&nbsp;<a title=\"Neuroimaging\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroimaging\">Neuroimaging</a>&nbsp;technologies that could deliver the necessary detailed understanding are improving rapidly, and&nbsp;<a title=\"Futurist\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Futurist\">futurist</a>&nbsp;<a title=\"Ray Kurzweil\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Kurzweil\">Ray Kurzweil</a>&nbsp;in the book&nbsp;<em>The Singularity Is Near</em><sup id=\"cite_ref-K_86-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-K-86\">[82]</a></sup>&nbsp;predicts that a map of sufficient quality will become available on a similar timescale to the computing power required to emulate it.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Early_estimates\" class=\"mw-headline\">Early estimates</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Early estimates\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Estimations_of_Human_Brain_Emulation_Required_Performance.svg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Estimations_of_Human_Brain_Emulation_Required_Performance.svg/478px-Estimations_of_Human_Brain_Emulation_Required_Performance.svg.png\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Estimations_of_Human_Brain_Emulation_Required_Performance.svg/717px-Estimations_of_Human_Brain_Emulation_Required_Performance.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Estimations_of_Human_Brain_Emulation_Required_Performance.svg/956px-Estimations_of_Human_Brain_Emulation_Required_Performance.svg.png 2x\" width=\"478\" height=\"359\" data-file-width=\"800\" data-file-height=\"600\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\nEstimates of how much processing power is needed to emulate a human brain at various levels (from Ray Kurzweil,&nbsp;<a title=\"Anders Sandberg\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anders_Sandberg\">Anders Sandberg</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Nick Bostrom\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Bostrom\">Nick Bostrom</a>), along with the fastest supercomputer from&nbsp;<a title=\"TOP500\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TOP500\">TOP500</a>&nbsp;mapped by year. Note the logarithmic scale and exponential trendline, which assumes the computational capacity doubles every 1.1 years. Kurzweil believes that mind uploading will be possible at neural simulation, while the Sandberg, Bostrom report is less certain about where&nbsp;<a title=\"Consciousness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness\">consciousness</a>&nbsp;arises.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandbergBostr&ouml;m2008_98-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandbergBostr%C3%B6m2008-98\">[94]</a></sup></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>For low-level brain simulation, an extremely powerful computer would be required. The&nbsp;<a title=\"Human brain\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_brain\">human brain</a>&nbsp;has a huge number of&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Synapses\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synapses\">synapses</a>. Each of the 10<sup>11</sup>&nbsp;(one hundred billion)&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Neurons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurons\">neurons</a>&nbsp;has on average 7,000 synaptic connections (synapses) to other neurons. The brain of a three-year-old child has about 10<sup>15</sup>&nbsp;synapses (1 quadrillion). This number declines with age, stabilizing by adulthood. Estimates vary for an adult, ranging from 10<sup>14</sup>&nbsp;to 5&times;10<sup>14</sup>&nbsp;synapses (100 to 500 trillion).<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrachman2005_99-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrachman2005-99\">[95]</a></sup>&nbsp;An estimate of the brain's processing power, based on a simple switch model for neuron activity, is around 10<sup>14</sup>&nbsp;(100 trillion) synaptic updates per second (<a title=\"SUPS\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SUPS\">SUPS</a>).<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003_100-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003-100\">[96]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 1997, Kurzweil looked at various estimates for the hardware required to equal the human brain and adopted a figure of 10<sup>16</sup>&nbsp;computations per second (cps).<sup id=\"cite_ref-103\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-103\">[e]</a></sup>&nbsp;(For comparison, if a \"computation\" was equivalent to one \"<a title=\"FLOPS\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FLOPS\">floating-point operation</a>\" &ndash; a measure used to rate current&nbsp;<a title=\"Supercomputer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supercomputer\">supercomputers</a>&nbsp;&ndash; then 10<sup>16</sup>&nbsp;\"computations\" would be equivalent to 10&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Peta-\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peta-\">petaFLOPS</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"FLOPS\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FLOPS#Performance_records\">achieved in 2011</a>, while 10<sup>18</sup>&nbsp;was&nbsp;<a title=\"Exascale computing\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exascale_computing\">achieved in 2022</a>.) He used this figure to predict the necessary hardware would be available sometime between 2015 and 2025, if the exponential growth in computer power at the time of writing continued.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Modelling_the_neurons_in_more_detail\" class=\"mw-headline\">Modelling the neurons in more detail</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Modelling the neurons in more detail\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>The&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial neuron\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neuron\">artificial neuron</a>&nbsp;model assumed by Kurzweil and used in many current&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial neural network\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network\">artificial neural network</a>&nbsp;implementations is simple compared with&nbsp;<a title=\"Biological neuron model\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_neuron_model\">biological neurons</a>. A brain simulation would likely have to capture the detailed cellular behaviour of biological&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Neurons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurons\">neurons</a>, presently understood only in broad outline. The overhead introduced by full modeling of the biological, chemical, and physical details of neural behaviour (especially on a molecular scale) would require computational powers several orders of magnitude larger than Kurzweil's estimate. In addition, the estimates do not account for&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Glial cells\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glial_cells\">glial cells</a>, which are known to play a role in cognitive processes.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Discover2011JanFeb_104-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Discover2011JanFeb-104\">[99]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Current_research\" class=\"mw-headline\">Current research</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Current research\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>Some research projects are investigating brain simulation using more sophisticated neural models, implemented on conventional computing architectures. The&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial Intelligence System\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_Intelligence_System\">Artificial Intelligence System</a>&nbsp;project implemented non-real time simulations of a \"brain\" (with 10<sup>11</sup>&nbsp;neurons) in 2005. It took 50 days on a cluster of 27 processors to simulate 1 second of a model.<sup id=\"cite_ref-105\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-105\">[100]</a></sup>&nbsp;The&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Blue Brain\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Brain\">Blue Brain</a>&nbsp;project used one of the fastest supercomputer architectures,&nbsp;<a title=\"IBM\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM\">IBM</a>'s&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Blue Gene\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Gene\">Blue Gene</a>&nbsp;platform, to create a real time simulation of a single rat&nbsp;<a title=\"Neocortex\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neocortex\">neocortical column</a>&nbsp;consisting of approximately 10,000 neurons and 10<sup>8</sup>&nbsp;synapses in 2006.<sup id=\"cite_ref-106\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-106\">[101]</a></sup>&nbsp;A longer-term goal is to build a detailed, functional simulation of the physiological processes in the human brain: \"It is not impossible to build a human brain and we can do it in 10 years,\"&nbsp;<a title=\"Henry Markram\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Markram\">Henry Markram</a>, director of the Blue Brain Project, said in 2009 at the&nbsp;<a title=\"TED (conference)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TED_(conference)\">TED conference</a>&nbsp;in Oxford.<sup id=\"cite_ref-107\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-107\">[102]</a></sup>&nbsp;Neuro-silicon interfaces have been proposed as an alternative implementation strategy that may scale better.<sup id=\"cite_ref-108\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-108\">[103]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p><a title=\"Hans Moravec\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Moravec\">Hans Moravec</a>&nbsp;addressed the above arguments (\"brains are more complicated\", \"neurons have to be modeled in more detail\") in his 1997 paper \"When will computer hardware match the human brain?\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoravec1998_102-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoravec1998-102\">[98]</a></sup>&nbsp;He measured the ability of existing software to simulate the functionality of neural tissue, specifically the retina. His results<sup class=\"noprint Inline-Template\">[<em><a title=\"Wikipedia:Citing sources\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources\"><span title=\"Statement needs to be more specific about the content to which it refers. (April 2023)\">specify</span></a></em>]</sup>&nbsp;do not depend on the number of glial cells, nor on what kinds of processing neurons perform where.</p>\r\n<p>The actual complexity of modeling biological neurons has been explored in&nbsp;<a title=\"OpenWorm\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenWorm\">OpenWorm project</a>&nbsp;that aimed at complete simulation of a worm that has only 302 neurons in its neural network (among about 1000 cells in total). The animal's neural network was well documented before the start of the project. However, although the task seemed simple at the beginning, the models based on a generic neural network did not work. Currently,<sup class=\"noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact\">[<em><a title=\"Portal:Current events\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portal:Current_events\"><span title=\"This statement refers to current events and needs references to newer reliable sources. (April 2023)\">may be outdated as of April 2023</span></a></em>]</sup>&nbsp;efforts focus on precise emulation of biological neurons (partly on the molecular level), but the result cannot yet be called a total success.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Criticisms_of_simulation-based_approaches\" class=\"mw-headline\">Criticisms of simulation-based approaches</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Criticisms of simulation-based approaches\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>A fundamental criticism of the simulated brain approach derives from&nbsp;<a title=\"Embodied cognition\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embodied_cognition\">embodied cognition</a>&nbsp;theory which asserts that human embodiment is an essential aspect of human intelligence and is necessary to ground meaning.<sup id=\"cite_ref-109\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-109\">[104]</a></sup>&nbsp;If this theory is correct, any fully functional brain model will need to encompass more than just the neurons (e.g., a robotic body). Goertzel<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoertzel2007_87-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoertzel2007-87\">[83]</a></sup>&nbsp;proposes virtual embodiment (like in&nbsp;<em><a title=\"Second Life\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Life\">Second Life</a></em>) as an option, but it is unknown whether this would be sufficient.</p>\r\n<p>Desktop computers using microprocessors capable of more than 10<sup>9</sup>&nbsp;cps (Kurzweil's non-standard unit \"computations per second\", see above) have been available since 2005. According to the brain power estimates used by Kurzweil (and Moravec), such a computer should be capable of supporting a simulation of a bee brain, but despite some interest<sup id=\"cite_ref-110\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-110\">[105]</a></sup>&nbsp;no such simulation exists.<sup class=\"noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact\">[<em><a title=\"Wikipedia:Citation needed\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed\"><span title=\"This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)\">citation needed</span></a></em>]</sup>&nbsp;There are several reasons for this:</p>\r\n<ol>\r\n<li>The neuron model seems to be oversimplified (see next section).</li>\r\n<li>There is insufficient understanding of higher cognitive processes<sup id=\"cite_ref-112\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-112\">[f]</a></sup>&nbsp;to establish accurately what the brain's neural activity (observed using techniques such as&nbsp;<a title=\"Neuroimaging\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroimaging#Functional_magnetic_resonance_imaging\">functional magnetic resonance imaging</a>) correlates with.</li>\r\n<li>Even if our understanding of cognition advances sufficiently, early simulation programs are likely to be very inefficient and will, therefore, need considerably more hardware.</li>\r\n<li>The brain of an organism, while critical, may not be an appropriate boundary for a cognitive model. To simulate a bee brain, it may be necessary to simulate the body, and the environment.&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"The Extended Mind\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Extended_Mind\">The Extended Mind</a>&nbsp;thesis formalises this philosophical concept, and research into&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Cephalopoda\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cephalopoda\">cephalopods</a>&nbsp;demonstrated clear examples of a decentralized system.<sup id=\"cite_ref-113\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-113\">[107]</a></sup></li>\r\n</ol>\r\n<p>In addition, the scale of the human brain is not currently well-constrained. One estimate puts the human brain at about 100 billion neurons and 100 trillion synapses.<sup id=\"cite_ref-114\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-114\">[108]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-115\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-115\">[109]</a></sup>&nbsp;Another estimate is 86 billion neurons of which 16.3 billion are in the&nbsp;<a title=\"Cerebral cortex\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerebral_cortex\">cerebral cortex</a>&nbsp;and 69 billion in the&nbsp;<a title=\"Cerebellum\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerebellum\">cerebellum</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAzevedo_et_al.2009_116-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAzevedo_et_al.2009-116\">[110]</a></sup>&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Glial cell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glial_cell\">Glial cell</a>&nbsp;synapses are currently unquantified but are known to be extremely numerous.</p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Philosophical_perspective\" class=\"mw-headline\">Philosophical perspective</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Philosophical perspective\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">See also:&nbsp;<a title=\"Philosophy of artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy_of_artificial_intelligence\">Philosophy of artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Turing test\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_test\">Turing test</a></div>\r\n<h3><span id=\".22Strong_AI.22_as_defined_in_philosophy\"></span><span id=\"&quot;Strong_AI&quot;_as_defined_in_philosophy\" class=\"mw-headline\">\"Strong AI\" as defined in philosophy</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: &quot;Strong AI&quot; as defined in philosophy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>In 1980, philosopher&nbsp;<a title=\"John Searle\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Searle\">John Searle</a>&nbsp;coined the term \"strong AI\" as part of his&nbsp;<a title=\"Chinese room\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_room\">Chinese room</a>&nbsp;argument.<sup id=\"cite_ref-117\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-117\">[111]</a></sup>&nbsp;He wanted to distinguish between two different hypotheses about artificial intelligence:<sup id=\"cite_ref-118\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-118\">[g]</a></sup></p>\r\n<ul>\r\n<li><strong>Strong AI hypothesis</strong>: An artificial intelligence system can \"think\"&mdash;have \"a mind\" and \"consciousness\".</li>\r\n<li><strong>Weak AI hypothesis</strong>: An artificial intelligence system can (only)&nbsp;<em>act like</em>&nbsp;it thinks and has a mind and consciousness.</li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>The first one he called \"strong\" because it makes a&nbsp;<em>stronger</em>&nbsp;statement: it assumes something special has happened to the machine that goes beyond those abilities that we can test. The behaviour of a \"weak AI\" machine would be precisely identical to a \"strong AI\" machine, but the latter would also have subjective conscious experience. This usage is also common in academic AI research and textbooks.<sup id=\"cite_ref-119\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-119\">[112]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Mainstream AI is most interested in how a program&nbsp;<em>behaves</em>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-120\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-120\">[113]</a></sup>&nbsp;According to&nbsp;<a title=\"Stuart J. Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stuart_J._Russell\">Russell</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Peter Norvig\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Norvig\">Norvig</a>, \"as long as the program works, they don't care if you call it real or a simulation.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003947_121-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003947-121\">[114]</a></sup>&nbsp;If the program can behave&nbsp;<em>as if</em>&nbsp;it has a mind, then there is no need to know if it&nbsp;<em>actually</em>&nbsp;has mind &ndash; indeed, there would be no way to tell. For AI research, Searle's \"weak AI hypothesis\" is equivalent to the statement \"artificial general intelligence is possible\". Thus, according to Russell and Norvig, \"most AI researchers take the weak AI hypothesis for granted, and don't care about the strong AI hypothesis.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003947_121-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003947-121\">[114]</a></sup>&nbsp;Thus, for academic AI research, \"Strong AI\" and \"AGI\" are two very different things.</p>\r\n<p>In contrast to Searle and mainstream AI, some futurists such as&nbsp;<a title=\"Ray Kurzweil\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Kurzweil\">Ray Kurzweil</a>&nbsp;use the term \"strong AI\" to mean \"human level artificial general intelligence\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-K_86-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-K-86\">[82]</a></sup>&nbsp;This is not the same as Searle's&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-disambig\" title=\"Strong AI\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strong_AI\">strong AI</a>, unless you assume that&nbsp;<a title=\"Consciousness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness\">consciousness</a>&nbsp;is necessary for human-level AGI. Academic philosophers such as Searle do not believe that is the case, and to most artificial intelligence researchers the question is out-of-scope.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003947_121-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003947-121\">[114]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Consciousness\"
