class=\"mw-headline\">Consciousness</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Consciousness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>Other aspects of the human mind besides intelligence are relevant to the concept of strong AI, and these play a major role in&nbsp;<a title=\"Science fiction\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_fiction\">science fiction</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a title=\"Ethics of artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethics_of_artificial_intelligence\">ethics of artificial intelligence</a>:</p>\r\n<ul>\r\n<li><a title=\"Consciousness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness\">consciousness</a>: To have&nbsp;<a title=\"Qualia\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qualia\">subjective experience</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"Thought\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thought\">thought</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-123\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-123\">[h]</a></sup></li>\r\n<li><a title=\"Self-awareness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-awareness\">self-awareness</a>: To be aware of oneself as a separate individual, especially to be aware of one's own thoughts.</li>\r\n<li><a title=\"Sentience\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sentience\">sentience</a>: The ability to \"feel\" perceptions or emotions subjectively.</li>\r\n<li><a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Sapience\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sapience\">sapience</a>: The capacity for wisdom.</li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p>These traits have a moral dimension, because a machine with this form of strong AI may have rights, analogous to the&nbsp;<a title=\"Animal rights\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_rights\">rights of non-human animals</a>. Preliminary work has been conducted on integrating&nbsp;<span class=\"cleanup-needed-content\">full ethical agents</span><sup class=\"noprint Inline-Template\">[<em><a title=\"Wikipedia:Please clarify\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify\"><span title=\"The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2023)\">clarification needed</span></a></em>]</sup>&nbsp;with existing legal and social frameworks, focusing on the legal position and rights of 'strong' AI.<sup id=\"cite_ref-physica_scripta_124-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-physica_scripta-124\">[116]</a></sup>&nbsp;<a title=\"Bill Joy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Joy\">Bill Joy</a>, among others, argues a machine with these traits may be a threat to human life or dignity.<sup id=\"cite_ref-125\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-125\">[117]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>It remains to be shown whether any of these traits are&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Necessary and sufficient condition\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Necessary_and_sufficient_condition\">necessary</a>&nbsp;for strong AI. The role of&nbsp;<a title=\"Consciousness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness\">consciousness</a>&nbsp;is not clear, and there is no agreed test for its presence. If a machine is built with a device that simulates the&nbsp;<a title=\"Neural correlates of consciousness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_correlates_of_consciousness\">neural correlates of consciousness</a>, would it automatically have self-awareness? It is possible that some of these traits&nbsp;<a title=\"Emergence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emergence\">naturally emerge</a>&nbsp;from a fully intelligent machine. It is also possible that people will&nbsp;<em>ascribe</em>&nbsp;these properties to machines once they begin to act in a way that is clearly intelligent.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Artificial_consciousness_research\" class=\"mw-headline\">Artificial consciousness research</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Artificial consciousness research\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article:&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial consciousness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_consciousness\">Artificial consciousness</a></div>\r\n<p>Although the role of consciousness in strong AI/AGI is debatable, many AGI researchers<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYudkowsky2006_111-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYudkowsky2006-111\">[106]</a></sup>&nbsp;regard research that investigates possibilities for implementing consciousness as vital. In an early effort&nbsp;<a title=\"Igor Aleksander\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Igor_Aleksander\">Igor Aleksander</a><sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAleksander1996_126-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAleksander1996-126\">[118]</a></sup>&nbsp;argued that the principles for creating a conscious machine already existed but that it would take forty years to train such a machine to understand&nbsp;<a title=\"Language\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language\">language</a>.<sup class=\"noprint Inline-Template\">[<em><a title=\"Wikipedia:Please clarify\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify\"><span title=\"The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2021)\">clarification needed</span></a></em>]</sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Research_challenges\" class=\"mw-headline\">Research challenges</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Research challenges\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">See also:&nbsp;<a title=\"History of artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_artificial_intelligence#The_problems\">History of artificial intelligence &sect;&nbsp;The problems</a>, and&nbsp;<a title=\"History of artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_artificial_intelligence#Predictions_(or_%22Where_is_HAL_9000?%22)\">History of artificial intelligence &sect;&nbsp;Predictions (or \"Where is HAL 9000?\")</a></div>\r\n<p>Progress in artificial intelligence has gone through periods of rapid progress separated by periods when progress appeared to stop.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClocksin2003_79-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClocksin2003-79\">[75]</a></sup>&nbsp;Ending each hiatus fundamental advances in hardware, software or both to create space for further progress.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClocksin2003_79-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClocksin2003-79\">[75]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-127\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-127\">[119]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-128\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-128\">[120]</a></sup>&nbsp;For example, the computer hardware available in the twentieth century was not sufficient to implement deep learning, which requires large numbers of GPU-enabled CPUs.<sup id=\"cite_ref-129\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-129\">[121]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The field has also oscillated between approaches to the problem. At times, effort has focused on explicit accumulation of facts and logic, as in&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Expert systems\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expert_systems\">expert systems</a>. At other times, systems were expected to build their own g via machine learning, as in artificial neural networks.<sup id=\"cite_ref-130\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-130\">[122]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>A further challenge is the lack of clarity in defining what&nbsp;<a title=\"Intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence\">intelligence</a>&nbsp;entails. Does it require consciousness? Must it display the ability to set goals as well as pursue them? Is it purely a matter of scale such that if model sizes increase sufficiently, intelligence will emerge? Are facilities such as planning, reasoning, and causal understanding required? Does intelligence require explicitly replicating the brain and its specific faculties? Does it require emotions?<sup id=\"cite_ref-131\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-131\">[123]</a></sup>&nbsp;<a title=\"David Gelernter\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Gelernter\">Gelernter</a>&nbsp;writes, \"No computer will be creative unless it can simulate all the nuances of human emotion.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelernter2010_132-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelernter2010-132\">[124]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-133\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-133\">[125]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-134\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-134\">[126]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Benefits\" class=\"mw-headline\">Benefits</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Benefits\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<p>AGI could have a wide variety of applications. If oriented towards such goal, AGI could help mitigate various problems in the world such as hunger, poverty and health problems.<sup id=\"cite_ref-135\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-135\">[127]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>AGI could improve the productivity and efficiency in most jobs. For example, in public health, AGI could accelerate medical research, notably against cancer.<sup id=\"cite_ref-136\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-136\">[128]</a></sup>&nbsp;It could take care of the elderly,<sup id=\"cite_ref-:8_137-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:8-137\">[129]</a></sup>&nbsp;and democratize access to rapid, high-quality medical diagnostics. It could offer fun, cheap and personalized education.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:8_137-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:8-137\">[129]</a></sup>&nbsp;For virtually any job that benefits society if done well, it would probably sooner or later be preferable to leave it to an AGI. The need to work to subsist could become obsolete if the wealth produced is properly redistributed.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:8_137-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:8-137\">[129]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:9_138-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:9-138\">[130]</a></sup>&nbsp;This also raises the question of the place of humans in a radically automated society.</p>\r\n<p>AGI could also help to make rational decisions, and to anticipate and prevent disasters. It could also help to reap the benefits of potentially catastrophic technologies such as&nbsp;<a title=\"Nanotechnology\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanotechnology\">nanotechnology</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title=\"Climate engineering\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_engineering\">climate engineering</a>, while avoiding the associated risks.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:7_139-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:7-139\">[131]</a></sup>&nbsp;If an AGI's primary goal is to prevent existential catastrophes such as human extinction (which could be difficult if the Vulnerable World Hypothesis turns out to be true<sup id=\"cite_ref-140\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-140\">[132]</a></sup>), it could take measures to drastically reduce the risks<sup id=\"cite_ref-:7_139-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:7-139\">[131]</a></sup>&nbsp;while minimizing the impact of these measures on our quality of life.</p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Risks\" class=\"mw-headline\">Risks</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Risks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Potential_threat_to_human_existence\" class=\"mw-headline\">Potential threat to human existence<span id=\"Risk_of_human_extinction\" class=\"anchor\"></span></span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Potential threat to human existence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main articles:&nbsp;<a title=\"Existential risk from artificial general intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Existential_risk_from_artificial_general_intelligence\">Existential risk from artificial general intelligence</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title=\"AI safety\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI_safety\">AI safety</a></div>\r\n<p>The thesis that AI poses an existential risk for humans, and that this risk needs much more attention than it currently gets, is controversial but has been endorsed by many public figures including&nbsp;<a title=\"Elon Musk\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk\">Elon Musk</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Bill Gates\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Gates\">Bill Gates</a>, and&nbsp;<a title=\"Stephen Hawking\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Hawking\">Stephen Hawking</a>. AI researchers like&nbsp;<a title=\"Stuart J. Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stuart_J._Russell\">Stuart J. Russell</a>,&nbsp;<a title=\"Roman Yampolskiy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Yampolskiy\">Roman Yampolskiy</a>, and Alexey Turchin, also support the basic thesis of a potential threat to humanity.<sup id=\"cite_ref-141\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-141\">[133]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-physica_scripta_124-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-physica_scripta-124\">[116]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-142\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-142\">[134]</a></sup>&nbsp;Gates states he does not \"understand why some people are not concerned\",<sup id=\"cite_ref-143\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-143\">[135]</a></sup>&nbsp;and Hawking criticized widespread indifference in his 2014 editorial:</p>\r\n<blockquote class=\"templatequote\">\r\n<p>So, facing possible futures of incalculable benefits and risks, the experts are surely doing everything possible to ensure the best outcome, right? Wrong. If a superior alien civilisation sent us a message saying, 'We'll arrive in a few decades,' would we just reply, 'OK, call us when you get here&ndash;we'll leave the lights on?' Probably not&ndash;but this is more or less what is happening with AI.<sup id=\"cite_ref-hawking_editorial_144-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-hawking_editorial-144\">[136]</a></sup></p>\r\n</blockquote>\r\n<p>The fate of humanity has sometimes been compared to the fate of gorillas threatened by human activities. Additional intelligence caused humanity to dominate gorillas, which are now vulnerable in ways that they could not have anticipated. The gorilla has become an endangered species, not out of malice, but simply as a collateral damage from human activities.<sup id=\"cite_ref-145\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-145\">[137]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The skeptic&nbsp;<a title=\"Yann LeCun\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yann_LeCun\">Yann LeCun</a>&nbsp;considers that AGIs will have no desire to dominate humanity and that we should be careful not to anthropomorphize them and interpret their intents as we would for humans. He said that people won't be \"smart enough to design super-intelligent machines, yet ridiculously stupid to the point of giving it moronic objectives with no safeguards\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-146\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-146\">[138]</a></sup>&nbsp;On the other side, the concept of&nbsp;<a title=\"Instrumental convergence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instrumental_convergence\">instrumental convergence</a>&nbsp;suggests that almost whatever their goals,&nbsp;<a title=\"Intelligent agent\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent\">intelligent agents</a>&nbsp;will have reasons to try to survive and acquire more power as intermediary steps to achieving these goals. And that this does not require having emotions.&nbsp;<a title=\"Nick Bostrom\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Bostrom\">Nick Bostrom</a>&nbsp;gives the thought experiment of the paper clips optimizer:<sup id=\"cite_ref-147\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-147\">[139]</a></sup></p>\r\n<blockquote class=\"templatequote\">\r\n<p>Suppose we have an AI whose only goal is to make as many paper clips as possible. The AI will realize quickly that it would be much better if there were no humans because humans might decide to switch it off. Because if humans do so, there would be fewer paper clips. Also, human bodies contain a lot of atoms that could be made into paper clips. The future that the AI would be trying to gear towards would be one in which there were a lot of paper clips but no humans.</p>\r\n</blockquote>\r\n<p>A 2021 systematic review of the risks associated with AGI, while noting the paucity of data, found the following potential threats: \"AGI removing itself from the control of human owners/managers, being given or developing unsafe goals, development of unsafe AGI, AGIs with poor ethics, morals and values; inadequate management of AGI, and existential risks\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-148\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-148\">[140]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Many scholars who are concerned about existential risk advocate (possibly massive) research into solving the difficult \"<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"AI control problem\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI_control_problem\">control problem</a>\" to answer the question: what types of safeguards, algorithms, or architectures can programmers implement to maximise the probability that their recursively-improving AI would continue to behave in a&nbsp;<a title=\"Friendly artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friendly_artificial_intelligence\">friendly</a>, rather than destructive, manner after it reaches superintelligence?<sup id=\"cite_ref-physica_scripta_124-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-physica_scripta-124\">[116]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-149\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-149\">[141]</a></sup>&nbsp;Solving the control problem is complicated by the AI arms race,<sup id=\"cite_ref-150\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-150\">[142]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-151\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-151\">[143]</a></sup>&nbsp;which will almost certainly see the militarization and weaponization of AGI by more than one nation-state, resulting in AGI-enabled warfare, and in the case of AI misalignment, AGI-directed warfare, potentially against all humanity.<sup id=\"cite_ref-152\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-152\">[144]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-153\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-153\">[145]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The thesis that AI can pose existential risk also has detractors. Skeptics sometimes charge that the thesis is crypto-religious, with an irrational belief in the possibility of superintelligence replacing an irrational belief in an omnipotent God.&nbsp;<a title=\"Jaron Lanier\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaron_Lanier\">Jaron Lanier</a>&nbsp;argued in 2014 that the idea that then-current machines were in any way intelligent is \"an illusion\" and a \"stupendous con\" by the wealthy.<sup id=\"cite_ref-atlantic-but-what_154-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-atlantic-but-what-154\">[146]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Much criticism argues that AGI is unlikely in the short term. Computer scientist&nbsp;<a title=\"Gordon Bell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gordon_Bell\">Gordon Bell</a>&nbsp;argues that the human race will destroy itself before it reaches the&nbsp;<a title=\"Technological singularity\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_singularity\">technological singularity</a>.&nbsp;<a title=\"Gordon Moore\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gordon_Moore\">Gordon Moore</a>, the original proponent of&nbsp;<a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Moore's Law\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moore%27s_Law\">Moore's Law</a>, declares: \"I am a skeptic. I don't believe [a technological singularity] is likely to happen, at least for a long time. And I don't know why I feel that way.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-155\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-155\">[147]</a></sup>&nbsp;Former&nbsp;<a title=\"Baidu\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baidu\">Baidu</a>&nbsp;Vice President and Chief Scientist&nbsp;<a title=\"Andrew Ng\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Ng\">Andrew Ng</a>&nbsp;said in 2015 that worrying about AI existential risk is \"like worrying about overpopulation on Mars when we have not even set foot on the planet yet.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-shermer_156-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-shermer-156\">[148]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-157\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-157\">[149]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2023, the CEOs of Google DeepMind, OpenAI and Anthropic, along with other industry leaders and researchers, issued a joint statement asserting that \"Mitigating the risk of extinction from AI should be a global priority alongside other societal-scale risks such as pandemics and nuclear war.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-158\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-158\">[150]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Mass_unemployment\" class=\"mw-headline\">Mass unemployment</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Mass unemployment\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\r\n<p>The job market is already impacted by current large language models. Researchers from OpenAI estimated that \"80% of the U.S. workforce could have at least 10% of their work tasks affected [...], while around 19% of workers may see at least 50% of their tasks impacted\" by the introduction of large language models like GPT-4.<sup id=\"cite_ref-159\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-159\">[151]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:6_160-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:6-160\">[152]</a></sup>&nbsp;Office workers seem to be the most impacted, notably mathematicians, accountants or web designers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:6_160-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:6-160\">[152]</a></sup>&nbsp;AGI could increase the autonomy of these systems, their ability to make decisions, to interface with other computer tools, but also to control robotized bodies.</p>\r\n<p>According to Stephen Hawking, this can be beneficial or harmful depending on how the wealth will be redistributed:<sup id=\"cite_ref-:9_138-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:9-138\">[130]</a></sup></p>\r\n<blockquote class=\"templatequote\">\r\n<p>Everyone can enjoy a life of luxurious leisure if the machine-produced wealth is shared, or most people can end up miserably poor if the machine-owners successfully lobby against wealth redistribution. So far, the trend seems to be toward the second option, with technology driving ever-increasing inequality</p>\r\n</blockquote>\r\n<p>Elon Musk considers that the automation of society will require governments to adopt a&nbsp;<a title=\"Universal basic income\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_basic_income\">universal basic income</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-161\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-161\">[153]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"See_also\" class=\"mw-headline\">See also</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: See also\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"div-col\">\r\n<ul>\r\n<li><a title=\"Artificial brain\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_brain\">Artificial brain</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Software and hardware with cognitive abilities similar to those of the animal or human brain</li>\r\n<li><a title=\"AI safety\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI_safety\">AI safety</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Research area on making AI safe and beneficial</li>\r\n<li><a title=\"AI alignment\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI_alignment\">AI alignment</a>&nbsp;&ndash; Conformance to the intended objective</li>\r\n<li><em><a title=\"A.I. class=\"mw-headline\">Notes</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: Notes\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"reflist reflist-lower-alpha\">\r\n<div class=\"mw-references-wrap\">\r\n<ol class=\"references\">\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-Searle's_Strong_AI-15\"><span class=\"mw-cite-backlink\">^&nbsp;<a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-Searle's_Strong_AI_15-0\"><span class=\"cite-accessibility-label\">Jump up to:</span><sup><em><strong>a</strong></em></sup></a>&nbsp;<a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-Searle's_Strong_AI_15-1\"><sup><em><strong>b</strong></em></sup></a></span>&nbsp;<span class=\"reference-text\">See below for the origin of the term \"strong AI\", and see the academic definition of \"<a title=\"Chinese room\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_room#Strong_AI\">strong AI</a>\" and weak AI in the article&nbsp;<a title=\"Chinese room\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_room\">Chinese room</a>.</span></li>\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-18\"><span class=\"mw-cite-backlink\"><strong><a title=\"Jump up\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-18\" aria-label=\"Jump up\">^</a></strong></span>&nbsp;<span class=\"reference-text\">AI founder&nbsp;<a title=\"John McCarthy (computer scientist)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_McCarthy_(computer_scientist)\">John McCarthy</a>&nbsp;writes: \"we cannot yet characterize in general what kinds of computational procedures we want to call intelligent.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-17\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-17\">[16]</a></sup>&nbsp;(For a discussion of some definitions of intelligence used by&nbsp;<a title=\"Artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence\">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;researchers, see&nbsp;<a title=\"Philosophy of artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy_of_artificial_intelligence\">philosophy of artificial intelligence</a>.)</span></li>\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-53\"><span class=\"mw-cite-backlink\"><strong><a title=\"Jump up\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-53\" aria-label=\"Jump up\">^</a></strong></span>&nbsp;<span class=\"reference-text\">The&nbsp;<a title=\"Lighthill report\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lighthill_report\">Lighthill report</a>&nbsp;specifically criticized AI's \"grandiose objectives\" and led the dismantling of AI research in England.<sup id=\"cite_ref-50\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-50\">[48]</a></sup>&nbsp;In the U.S.,&nbsp;<a title=\"DARPA\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DARPA\">DARPA</a>&nbsp;became determined to fund only \"mission-oriented direct research, rather than basic undirected research\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTENRC1999&quot;Shift_to_Applied_Research_Increases_Investment&quot;_51-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTENRC1999%22Shift_to_Applied_Research_Increases_Investment%22-51\">[49]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-52\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-52\">[50]</a></sup></span></li>\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-58\"><span class=\"mw-cite-backlink\"><strong><a title=\"Jump up\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-58\" aria-label=\"Jump up\">^</a></strong></span>&nbsp;<span class=\"reference-text\">As AI founder&nbsp;<a title=\"John McCarthy (computer scientist)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_McCarthy_(computer_scientist)\">John McCarthy</a>&nbsp;writes \"it would be a great relief to the rest of the workers in AI if the inventors of new general formalisms would express their hopes in a more guarded form than has sometimes been the case.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-57\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-57\">[54]</a></sup></span></li>\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-103\"><span class=\"mw-cite-backlink\"><strong><a title=\"Jump up\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-103\" aria-label=\"Jump up\">^</a></strong></span>&nbsp;<span class=\"reference-text\">In \"Mind Children\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoravec198861_101-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoravec198861-101\">[97]</a></sup>&nbsp;10<sup>15</sup>&nbsp;cps is used. More recently, in 1997,<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoravec1998_102-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoravec1998-102\">[98]</a></sup>&nbsp;Moravec argued for 10<sup>8</sup>&nbsp;MIPS which would roughly correspond to 10<sup>14</sup>&nbsp;cps. Moravec talks in terms of MIPS, not \"cps\", which is a non-standard term Kurzweil introduced.</span></li>\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-112\"><span class=\"mw-cite-backlink\"><strong><a title=\"Jump up\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-112\" aria-label=\"Jump up\">^</a></strong></span>&nbsp;<span class=\"reference-text\">In Goertzels' AGI book, Yudkowsky proposes 5 levels of organisation that must be understood &ndash; code/data, sensory modality, concept &amp; category, thought, and deliberation (consciousness) &ndash; in order to use the available hardware.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYudkowsky2006_111-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYudkowsky2006-111\">[106]</a></sup></span></li>\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-118\"><span class=\"mw-cite-backlink\"><strong><a title=\"Jump up\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-118\" aria-label=\"Jump up\">^</a></strong></span>&nbsp;<span class=\"reference-text\">As defined in a standard AI textbook: \"The assertion that machines could possibly act intelligently (or, perhaps better, act as if they were intelligent) is called the 'weak AI' hypothesis by philosophers, and the assertion that machines that do so are actually thinking (as opposed to simulating thinking) is called the 'strong AI' hypothesis.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003_100-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTERussellNorvig2003-100\">[96]</a></sup></span></li>\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-123\"><span class=\"mw-cite-backlink\"><strong><a title=\"Jump up\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-123\" aria-label=\"Jump up\">^</a></strong></span>&nbsp;<span class=\"reference-text\">Note that&nbsp;<a title=\"Consciousness\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness\">consciousness</a>&nbsp;is difficult to define. A popular definition, due to&nbsp;<a title=\"Thomas Nagel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Nagel\">Thomas Nagel</a>, is that it \"feels like\" something to be conscious. If we are not conscious, then it doesn't feel like anything. Nagel uses the example of a bat: we can sensibly ask \"what does it feel like to be a bat?\" However, we are unlikely to ask \"what does it feel like to be a toaster?\" Nagel concludes that a bat appears to be conscious (i.e. has consciousness) but a toaster does not.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTENagel1974_122-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTENagel1974-122\">[115]</a></sup></span></li>\r\n</ol>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<h2><span id=\"References\" class=\"mw-headline\">References</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a title=\"Edit section: References\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"reflist reflist-columns references-column-width\">\r\n<ol class=\"references\">\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-1\"><span class=\"mw-cite-backlink\"><strong><a title=\"Jump up\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_ref-1\" aria-label=\"Jump up\">^</a></strong></span>&nbsp;<span class=\"reference-text\"><cite id=\"CITEREFHodson2019\" class=\"citation news cs1\">Hodson, Hal (1 March 2019).&nbsp;<a class=\"external text\" href=\"https://www.economist.com/1843/2019/03/01/deepmind-and-google-the-battle-to-control-artificial-intelligence\" rel=\"nofollow\">\"DeepMind and Google: the battle to control artificial intelligence\"</a>.&nbsp;<em><a title=\"1843 (magazine)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1843_(magazine)\">1843</a></em>.&nbsp;<a class=\"external text\" href=\"https://web.archive.org/web/20200707223031/https://www.economist.com/1843/2019/03/01/deepmind-and-google-the-battle-to-control-artificial-intelligence\" rel=\"nofollow\">Archived</a>&nbsp;from the original on 7 July 2020<span class=\"reference-accessdate\">. likes: []
name: "Artificial General Intelligence (AGI)"
tagline: "Skynet otw"
tags: ["v279zcrn3qjme3j","b0uoqk121pmlyfi"]
thumbnail: "modern_tech_5szoAYiOq5.png"
updated: "2023-06-20 20:02:13.818Z"
url: "https://google.com"
user: "8ti99kn9yavd7mb"
expand: {}
---

<p>An&nbsp;<strong>artificial general intelligence</strong>&nbsp;(<strong>AGI</strong>) is a type of hypothetical&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agent</a>. The AGI concept is that it can learn to accomplish any intellectual task that&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Human beings" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_beings">human beings</a>&nbsp;or animals can perform.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_2-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:10-2">[2]</a></sup>&nbsp;Alternatively, AGI has been defined as an autonomous system that surpasses human capabilities in the majority of economically valuable tasks.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_3-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:1-3">[3]</a></sup>&nbsp;Creating AGI is a primary goal of some&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;research and companies such as&nbsp;<a title="OpenAI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenAI">OpenAI</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:1-3">[3]</a></sup>&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="DeepMind" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeepMind">DeepMind</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Anthropic" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthropic">Anthropic</a>. AGI is a common topic in&nbsp;<a title="Science fiction" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_fiction">science fiction</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Futures studies" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Futures_studies">futures studies</a>.</p>
<p>The timeline for AGI development remains a subject of ongoing debate among researchers and experts. Some argue that it may be possible in years or decades, others maintain it might take a century or longer, and a minority believe it may never be achieved.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_5-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:2-5">[5]</a></sup>&nbsp;Additionally, there is debate regarding whether modern deep learning systems, such as&nbsp;<a title="GPT-4" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GPT-4">GPT-4</a>, are an early yet incomplete form of AGI<sup id="cite_ref-:11_6-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:11-6">[6]</a></sup>&nbsp;or if new approaches are required.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_7-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:3-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Contention exists over the potential for AGI to pose a threat to humanity; for example, OpenAI treats it as an&nbsp;<a title="Existential risk from artificial general intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Existential_risk_from_artificial_general_intelligence">existential risk</a>, while others find the development of AGI to be too remote to present a risk.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_5-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:2-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_7-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:3-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2020 survey identified 72 active AGI&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;D" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%26D">R&amp;D</a>&nbsp;projects spread across 37 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-baum_9-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-baum-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="Terminology" class="mw-headline">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Terminology" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>AGI is also known as strong AI,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKurzweil2005260_10-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKurzweil2005260-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kurzweil_2005-08-05_11-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Kurzweil_2005-08-05-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>&nbsp;full AI,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>&nbsp;or general intelligent action.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENewellSimon1976_14-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTENewellSimon1976-14">[14]</a></sup>&nbsp;However, some academic sources reserve the term "strong AI" for computer programs that experience&nbsp;<a title="Sentience" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sentience">sentience</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Consciousness" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness">consciousness</a>.&nbsp;<sup id="cite_ref-Searle's_Strong_AI_15-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Searle's_Strong_AI-15">[a]</a></sup>&nbsp;In contrast, weak AI (or narrow AI) is able to solve one specific problem, but lacks general cognitive abilities.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kurzweil_2005-08-05_11-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Kurzweil_2005-08-05-11">[11]</a></sup>&nbsp;Some academic sources use "weak AI" to refer more broadly to any programs that neither experience consciousness nor have a mind in the same sense as humans.<sup id="cite_ref-Searle's_Strong_AI_15-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Searle's_Strong_AI-15">[a]</a></sup></p>
<p>Related concepts include human-level AI, transformative AI,<sup id="cite_ref-:2_5-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:2-5">[5]</a></sup>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Superintelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superintelligence">superintelligence</a>.</p>
<h2><span id="Characteristics" class="mw-headline">Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Characteristics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article:&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">Artificial intelligence</a></div>
<p>Various criteria for&nbsp;<a title="Intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence">intelligence</a>&nbsp;have been proposed (most famously the&nbsp;<a title="Turing test" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_test">Turing test</a>) but no definition is broadly accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-18">[b]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Intelligence_traits" class="mw-headline">Intelligence traits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Intelligence traits" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>However, researchers generally hold that intelligence is required to do the following:<sup id="cite_ref-:12_19-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:12-19">[17]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a title="Automated reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning">reason</a>, use strategy, solve puzzles, and make judgments under&nbsp;<a title="Uncertainty" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncertainty">uncertainty</a>;</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Knowledge representation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_representation">represent knowledge</a>, including&nbsp;<a title="Commonsense knowledge (artificial intelligence)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonsense_knowledge_(artificial_intelligence)">common sense knowledge</a>;</li>
<li><a title="Automated planning and scheduling" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_planning_and_scheduling">plan</a>;</li>
<li><a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">learn</a>;</li>
<li>communicate in&nbsp;<a title="Natural language processing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_processing">natural language</a>;</li>
</ul>
<p>and, if necessary,&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence systems integration" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence_systems_integration">integrate these skills</a>&nbsp;in completion of any given goal.</p>
<p>Many&nbsp;<a title="Interdisciplinarity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinarity">interdisciplinary</a>&nbsp;approaches (e.g.&nbsp;<a title="Cognitive science" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_science">cognitive science</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Computational intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_intelligence">computational intelligence</a>, and&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Decision making" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_making">decision making</a>) consider additional traits such as&nbsp;<a title="Imagination" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imagination">imagination</a>&nbsp;(the ability to form novel mental images and concepts)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Self-determination theory" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-determination_theory">autonomy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Computer-based systems that exhibit many of these capabilities exist (e.g. see&nbsp;<a title="Computational creativity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computational_creativity">computational creativity</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Automated reasoning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_reasoning">automated reasoning</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Decision support system" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_support_system">decision support system</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Robot" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robot">robot</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Evolutionary computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computation">evolutionary computation</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Intelligent agent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligent_agent">intelligent agent</a>). However, no consensus holds that modern AI systems possess them to an adequate degree.</p>
<h3><span id="Physical_traits" class="mw-headline">Physical traits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Physical traits" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Other capabilities are considered desirable in intelligent systems, as they may affect intelligence or aid in its expression. These include:<sup id="cite_ref-:13_22-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:13-22">[20]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>the ability to&nbsp;<a title="Machine perception" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_perception">sense</a>&nbsp;(e.g.&nbsp;<a title="Computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision">see</a>, hear, etc.), and</li>
<li>the ability to act (e.g.&nbsp;<a title="Robotics" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics">move and manipulate objects</a>, change location to explore, etc.)</li>
</ul>
<p>This includes the ability to detect and respond to&nbsp;<a title="Hazard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazard">hazard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Mathematical_formalisms" class="mw-headline">Mathematical formalisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Mathematical formalisms" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A mathematically precise specification of AGI was proposed by&nbsp;<a title="Marcus Hutter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Hutter">Marcus Hutter</a>&nbsp;in 2000. Named&nbsp;<a title="AIXI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AIXI">AIXI</a>, the proposed AGI agent maximises &ldquo;the ability to satisfy goals in a wide range of environments&rdquo;.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_24-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:14-24">[22]</a></sup>&nbsp;This type of AGI, characterized by the ability to maximise a mathematical definition of intelligence rather than exhibit human-like behaviour,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup>&nbsp;is also called universal artificial intelligence.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Jan Lieke (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jan_Lieke&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Jan Lieke</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Marcus Hutter" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Hutter">Marcus Hutter</a>&nbsp;showed that Legg-Hutter intelligence - "an agent&rsquo;s ability to achieve goals in a wide range of environments"<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup>&nbsp;- is measured with respect to "a fixed Universal Turing Machine<a title="Universal Turing machine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Turing_machine">(UTM</a>). AIXI is the most intelligent policy if it uses the same UTM", a result which "undermines all existing optimality properties for AIXI".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup>&nbsp;This problem stems from AIXI's use of compression as a proxy for intelligence, which is only valid if cognition takes place in isolation from the environment in which goals are pursued. This formalises a philosophical position known as&nbsp;<a title="Mind&ndash;body dualism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind%E2%80%93body_dualism">Mind&ndash;body dualism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-&rdquo;mtb1&rdquo;_29-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-%E2%80%9Dmtb1%E2%80%9D-29">[27]</a></sup>&nbsp;Some find&nbsp;<a title="Enactivism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enactivism">enactivism</a>&nbsp;more plausible&mdash;the notion that cognition takes place within the same environment in which goals are pursued.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup>&nbsp;Subsequently,&nbsp;<a class="new" title="Michael Timothy Bennett (page does not exist)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Michael_Timothy_Bennett&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1">Michael Timothy Bennett</a>&nbsp;formalised enactive cognition and identified an alternative proxy for intelligence called "weakness".<sup id="cite_ref-&rdquo;mtb1&rdquo;_29-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-%E2%80%9Dmtb1%E2%80%9D-29">[27]</a></sup>&nbsp;The accompanying experiments (comparing weakness and compression) and mathematical proofs showed that maximising weakness results in the optimal "ability to complete a wide range of tasks"<sup id="cite_ref-&rdquo;mtb2&rdquo;_31-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-%E2%80%9Dmtb2%E2%80%9D-31">[29]</a></sup>&nbsp;or equivalently "ability to generalise"<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup>&nbsp;(thus maximising intelligence by either definition). If&nbsp;<a title="Enactivism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enactivism">enactivism</a>&nbsp;holds and&nbsp;<a title="Mind&ndash;body dualism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind%E2%80%93body_dualism">Mind&ndash;body dualism</a>&nbsp;does not, then compression is not necessary or sufficient for intelligence, calling into question widely held views on intelligence (see also&nbsp;<a title="Hutter Prize" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hutter_Prize">Hutter Prize</a>).</p>
<p>Whether an AGI that satisfies one of these formalizations exhibits human-like behaviour (such as the use of natural language) would depend on many factors,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup>&nbsp;for example the manner in which the agent is embodied,<sup id="cite_ref-&rdquo;mtb2&rdquo;_31-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-%E2%80%9Dmtb2%E2%80%9D-31">[29]</a></sup>&nbsp;or whether it has a reward function that closely approximates human primitives of cognition like hunger, pain, and so forth.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Tests_for_testing_human-level_AGI" class="mw-headline">Tests for testing human-level AGI<span id="Tests_for_confirming_human-level_AGI" class="anchor"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Tests for testing human-level AGI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several tests meant to confirm human-level AGI have been considered, including:<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt><a title="Turing test" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_test">The Turing Test</a>&nbsp;(<a title="Alan Turing" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Turing"><em>Turing</em></a>)</dt>
<dd>A machine and a human both converse unseen with a second human, who must evaluate which of the two is the machine, which passes the test if it can fool the evaluator a significant fraction of the time. Note: Turing does not prescribe what should qualify as intelligence, only that knowing that it is a machine should disqualify it. The AI&nbsp;<a title="Eugene Goostman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eugene_Goostman">Eugene Goostman</a>&nbsp;achieved Turing's estimate of convincing 30% of judges that it was human in 2014.</dd>
<dt>The Robot College Student Test (<a title="Ben Goertzel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Goertzel"><em>Goertzel</em></a>)</dt>
<dd>A machine enrolls in a university, taking and passing the same classes that humans would, and obtaining a degree. LLMs can now pass university degree-level exams without even attending the classes.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup></dd>
<dt>The Employment Test (<a title="Nils John Nilsson" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nils_John_Nilsson"><em>Nilsson</em></a>)</dt>
<dd>A machine performs an economically important job at least as well as humans in the same job. AIs are now replacing humans in many roles as varied as fast food, marketing, and software engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup></dd>
<dt>The Ikea test (<a title="Gary Marcus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gary_Marcus"><em>Marcus</em></a>)</dt>
<dd>Also known as the Flat Pack Furniture Test. An AI views the parts and instructions of an Ikea flat-pack product, then controls a robot to assemble the furniture correctly.</dd>
<dt>The Coffee Test (<a title="Steve Wozniak" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Wozniak"><em>Wozniak</em></a>)</dt>
<dd>A machine is required to enter an average American home and figure out how to make coffee: find the coffee machine, find the coffee, add water, find a mug, and brew the coffee by pushing the proper buttons. This has not yet been completed.</dd>
</dl>
<p>As each test is completed it is supplanted with others. The current state is that generalist AIs can surpass most trained humans at arbitrary degree-level exams, score in the top 0.1% of IQ tests,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup>&nbsp;and be so Turing-convincing that some of their own developers believe they're sentient,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup>&nbsp;all of which are general tasks for which they were not specifically trained, and yet the AIs are still not considered "generally intelligent"&nbsp;<em>enough</em>&nbsp;to be AGI.</p>
<h3><span id="AI-complete_problems" class="mw-headline">AI-complete problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: AI-complete problems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article:&nbsp;<a title="AI-complete" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AI-complete">AI-complete</a></div>
<p>There are many problems that may require general intelligence, if machines are to solve the problems as well as people do. For example, even specific straightforward tasks, like&nbsp;<a title="Machine translation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_translation">machine translation</a>, require that a machine read and write in both languages (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#Natural_language_processing">NLP</a>), follow the author's argument (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#Deduction,_reasoning,_problem_solving">reason</a>), know what is being talked about (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#Knowledge_representation">knowledge</a>), and faithfully reproduce the author's original intent (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#Social_intelligence">social intelligence</a>). All of these problems need to be solved simultaneously in order to reach human-level machine performance.</p>
<p>A problem is informally called "AI-complete" or "AI-hard" if it is believed that to solve it one would need to implement strong AI, because the solution is beyond the capabilities of a purpose-specific algorithm.<sup id="cite_ref-Shapiro92_41-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-Shapiro92-41">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>AI-complete problems are hypothesised to include general&nbsp;<a title="Computer vision" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision">computer vision</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Natural-language understanding" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural-language_understanding">natural language understanding</a>, and dealing with unexpected circumstances while solving any real-world problem.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>AI-complete problems cannot be solved with current<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact">[<em><a title="Portal:Current events" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portal:Current_events"><span title="This statement refers to current events and needs references to newer reliable sources. (April 2023)">may be outdated as of April 2023</span></a></em>]</sup>&nbsp;computer technology alone, and require&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Human computation" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_computation">human computation</a>. This limitation could be useful to test for the presence of humans, as&nbsp;<a title="CAPTCHA" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CAPTCHA">CAPTCHAs</a>&nbsp;aim to do; and for&nbsp;<a title="Computer security" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_security">computer security</a>&nbsp;to repel&nbsp;<a title="Brute-force attack" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brute-force_attack">brute-force attacks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="History" class="mw-headline">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: History" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Classical_AI" class="mw-headline">Classical AI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Classical AI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles:&nbsp;<a title="History of artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_artificial_intelligence">History of artificial intelligence</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Symbolic artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbolic_artificial_intelligence">Symbolic artificial intelligence</a></div>
<p>Modern AI research began in the mid-1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup>&nbsp;The first generation of AI researchers were convinced that artificial general intelligence was possible and that it would exist in just a few decades.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup>&nbsp;AI pioneer&nbsp;<a title="Herbert A. Simon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_A._Simon">Herbert A. Simon</a>&nbsp;wrote in 1965: "machines will be capable, within twenty years, of doing any work a man can do."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Their predictions were the inspiration for&nbsp;<a title="Stanley Kubrick" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick">Stanley Kubrick</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Arthur C. Clarke" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_C._Clarke">Arthur C. Clarke</a>'s character&nbsp;<a title="HAL 9000" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HAL_9000">HAL 9000</a>, who embodied what AI researchers believed they could create by the year 2001. AI pioneer&nbsp;<a title="Marvin Minsky" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvin_Minsky">Marvin Minsky</a>&nbsp;was a consultant<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup>&nbsp;on the project of making HAL 9000 as realistic as possible according to the consensus predictions of the time. He said in 1967, "Within a generation... the problem of creating 'artificial intelligence' will substantially be solved".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Symbolic AI" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbolic_AI">classical AI projects</a>, such as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Doug Lenat" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doug_Lenat">Doug Lenat</a>'s&nbsp;<a title="Cyc" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyc">Cyc</a>&nbsp;project (that began in 1984), and&nbsp;<a title="Allen Newell" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allen_Newell">Allen Newell</a>'s&nbsp;<a title="Soar (cognitive architecture)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soar_(cognitive_architecture)">Soar</a>&nbsp;project, were directed at AGI.</p>
<p>However, in the early 1970s, it became obvious that researchers had grossly underestimated the difficulty of the project. Funding agencies became skeptical of AGI and put researchers under increasing pressure to produce useful "applied AI".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-53">[c]</a></sup>&nbsp;In the early 1980s, Japan's&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Fifth Generation Computer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fifth_Generation_Computer">Fifth Generation Computer</a>&nbsp;Project revived interest in AGI, setting out a ten-year timeline that included AGI goals like "carry on a casual conversation".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup>&nbsp;In response to this and the success of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Expert systems" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expert_systems">expert systems</a>, both industry and government pumped money back into the field.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENRC1999&quot;Shift_to_Applied_Research_Increases_Investment&quot;_51-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-FOOTNOTENRC1999%22Shift_to_Applied_Research_Increases_Investment%22-51">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup>&nbsp;However, confidence in AI spectacularly collapsed in the late 1980s, and the goals of the Fifth Generation Computer Project were never fulfilled.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup>&nbsp;For the second time in 20 years, AI researchers who predicted the imminent achievement of AGI had been mistaken. By the 1990s, AI researchers had a reputation for making vain promises. They became reluctant to make predictions at all<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-58">[d]</a></sup>&nbsp;and avoided mention of "human level" artificial intelligence for fear of being labeled "wild-eyed dreamer[s]".<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-59">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Narrow_AI_research" class="mw-headline">Narrow AI research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Narrow AI research" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article:&nbsp;<a title="Artificial intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence">Artificial intelligence</a></div>
<p>In the 1990s and early 21st century, mainstream AI achieved commercial success and academic respectability by focusing on specific sub-problems where AI can produce verifiable results and commercial applications, such as&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Artificial neural networks" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_networks">artificial neural networks</a>&nbsp;and statistical&nbsp;<a title="Machine learning" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning">machine learning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-60">[56]</a></sup>&nbsp;These "applied AI" systems are now used extensively throughout the technology industry, and research in this vein is heavily funded in both academia and industry. As of 2018&nbsp;development on this field was considered an emerging trend, and a mature stage was expected to happen in more than 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most mainstream AI researchers<sup id="cite_ref-:4_62-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:4-62">[58]</a></sup>&nbsp;hope that strong AI can be developed by combining programs that solve various sub-problems.&nbsp;<a title="Hans Moravec" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Moravec">Hans Moravec</a>&nbsp;wrote in 1988:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>I am confident that this bottom-up route to artificial intelligence will one day meet the traditional top-down route more than half way, ready to provide the real world competence and the&nbsp;<a title="Commonsense knowledge (artificial intelligence)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonsense_knowledge_(artificial_intelligence)">commonsense knowledge</a>&nbsp;that has been so frustratingly elusive in reasoning programs. Fully intelligent machines will result when the metaphorical&nbsp;<a title="Golden spike" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_spike">golden spike</a>&nbsp;is driven uniting the two efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_62-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-:4-62">[58]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>However, this is disputed. For example, Stevan Harnad of Princeton University concluded his 1990 paper on the&nbsp;<a title="Symbol grounding problem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symbol_grounding_problem">Symbol Grounding Hypothesis</a>&nbsp;by stating:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The expectation has often been voiced that "top-down" (symbolic) approaches to modeling cognition will somehow meet "bottom-up" (sensory) approaches somewhere in between. If the grounding considerations in this paper are valid, then this expectation is hopelessly modular and there is really only one viable route from sense to symbols: from the ground up. A free-floating symbolic level like the software level of a computer will never be reached by this route (or vice versa) &ndash; nor is it clear why we should even try to reach such a level, since it looks as if getting there would just amount to uprooting our symbols from their intrinsic meanings (thereby merely reducing ourselves to the functional equivalent of a programmable computer).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-63">[59]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span id="Modern_artificial_general_intelligence_research" class="mw-headline">Modern artificial general intelligence research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Modern artificial general intelligence research" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The term "artificial general intelligence" was used as early as 1997, by Mark Gubrud<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-64">[60]</a></sup>&nbsp;in a discussion of the implications of fully automated military production and operations. The term was re-introduced and popularized by&nbsp;<a title="Shane Legg" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shane_Legg">Shane Legg</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Ben Goertzel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Goertzel">Ben Goertzel</a>&nbsp;around 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-65">[61]</a></sup>&nbsp;AGI research activity in 2006 was described by Pei Wang and Ben Goertzel<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-66">[62]</a></sup>&nbsp;as "producing publications and preliminary results". The first summer school in AGI was organized in Xiamen, China in 2009<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-67">[63]</a></sup>&nbsp;by the Xiamen university's Artificial Brain Laboratory and OpenCog. The first university course was given in 2010<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-68">[64]</a></sup>&nbsp;and 2011<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup>&nbsp;at Plovdiv University, Bulgaria by Todor Arnaudov. MIT presented a course in AGI in 2018, organized by&nbsp;<a title="Lex Fridman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lex_Fridman">Lex Fridman</a>&nbsp;and featuring a number of guest lecturers.</p>
<p>As of 2023, a small number of computer scientists are active in AGI research, and many contribute to a series of&nbsp;<a title="Conference on Artificial General Intelligence" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conference_on_Artificial_General_Intelligence">AGI conferences</a>. However, increasingly more researchers are interested in open-ended learning<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-71">[67]</a></sup>, which is the idea of allowing AI to continuously learn and innovate like humans do. Although most open-ended learning works are still done on&nbsp;<a title="Minecraft" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minecraft">Minecraft</a><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-73">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup>, its application can be extended to robotics and the sciences.</p>
<h3><span id="Feasibility" class="mw-headline">Feasibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Edit section: Feasibility" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artificial_general_intelligence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2022, AGI remains speculative.<sup id="cite_ref-spec1_75-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-spec1-75">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spec2_76-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence#cite_note-spec2-76">[72]</a></sup>&nbsp;No such system has yet been demonstrated. Opinions vary both on whether and when artificial general intelligence will arrive. AI pioneer&nbsp;<a title="Herbert A. Simon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_A._Simon">Herbert A. Simon</a>&nbsp;speculated in 1965 that "machines will be capable, within twenty years, of doing any work a man can do". This prediction failed to come true.
